      <p class="min-height"><b>From the Business:</b>Wah Jee Wah  is an Indian catering company that serves the San Francisco Bay Area market. We cater to a variety of options apart from the conventional  indian dishes in the market .Wah jee wah has been in business for over 18 years , providing services for weddings , birthdays , festivals, corporate events etc .Offering up live stations of street foods , gourmet, protein &amp; veg right off the grill , custom equipment using only the best sourced ingredients. Offering industry standard and home style cooking . Our head chef Rounak Dumra , started his career as a young boy working for his family restaurant in the town of Fremont, 30-45 mins from sf downtown. Wah jee wah started by his father Anil s Dumra  made great name in the community and thrived on catering business, with 40+ years in the business. Rounak Dumra after working for his father for several years. Time magazine says: Indian food is lauded for its curries, mouth-burning spices and complex flavor pairings. With its use of cardamom, cayenne, tamarind, and other pungent ingredients, the resulting taste combinations are unlike anything found elsewhere around the world. But scientists in India have now discovered exactly why Indian food is so good — it’s the fewer number of overlapping flavors in ingredients. Researchers at the Indian Institute for Technology examined how frequently overlapping flavor compounds factored into a dish’s ingredients. They reviewed thousands of recipes on TarlaDalal.com, scrutinizing the subtle molecular-level differences that distinguish the cuisine, reports the Washington Post. “We found that average flavor sharing in Indian cuisine was significantly lesser than expected,” researchers wrote. In Western cuisines, ingredients are usually paired together for their similar flavors. However, an average Indian dish includes at least seven ingredients, most of which do not contain overlapping flavors. Cayenne, green bell pepper, coriander, and gram masala are usually paired with ingredients that have no chemical overlap, but each ingredient brings a unique component when incorporated into the final meal. This creates knockout dishes for cuisine that uses approximately 200 of the estimated 381 ingredients known in the world.<span class="more-links" style="display: none;"><a title="Read More about India Gourmet" href="javascript:void()" onclick="javascript:openFullDescriptionWeb(this)">Read more</a></span></p>
